<line act="1" scene="1" line="1" speaker="First Citizen">Before we proceed any further, hear me speak.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="2" speaker="All">Speak, speak.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="3" speaker="First Citizen">You are all resolved rather to die than to famish?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="4" speaker="All">Resolved. resolved.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="5" speaker="First Citizen">First, you know Caius Marcius is chief enemy to the people.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="6" speaker="All">We know't, we know't.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="7" speaker="First Citizen">Let us kill him, and we'll have corn at our own price.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="8" speaker="First Citizen">Is't a verdict?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="9" speaker="All">No more talking on't; let it be done: away, away!</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="10" speaker="Second Citizen">One word, good citizens.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="11" speaker="First Citizen">We are accounted poor citizens, the patricians good.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="12" speaker="First Citizen">What authority surfeits on would relieve us: if they</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="13" speaker="First Citizen">would yield us but the superfluity, while it were</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="14" speaker="First Citizen">wholesome, we might guess they relieved us humanely;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="15" speaker="First Citizen">but they think we are too dear: the leanness that</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="16" speaker="First Citizen">afflicts us, the object of our misery, is as an</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="17" speaker="First Citizen">inventory to particularise their abundance; our</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="18" speaker="First Citizen">sufferance is a gain to them Let us revenge this with</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="19" speaker="First Citizen">our pikes, ere we become rakes: for the gods know I</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="20" speaker="First Citizen">speak this in hunger for bread, not in thirst for revenge.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="21" speaker="Second Citizen">Would you proceed especially against Caius Marcius?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="22" speaker="All">Against him first: he's a very dog to the commonalty.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="23" speaker="Second Citizen">Consider you what services he has done for his country?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="24" speaker="First Citizen">Very well; and could be content to give him good</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="25" speaker="First Citizen">report fort, but that he pays himself with being proud.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="26" speaker="Second Citizen">Nay, but speak not maliciously.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="27" speaker="First Citizen">I say unto you, what he hath done famously, he did</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="28" speaker="First Citizen">it to that end: though soft-conscienced men can be</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="29" speaker="First Citizen">content to say it was for his country he did it to</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="30" speaker="First Citizen">please his mother and to be partly proud; which he</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="31" speaker="First Citizen">is, even till the altitude of his virtue.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="32" speaker="Second Citizen">What he cannot help in his nature, you account a</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="33" speaker="Second Citizen">vice in him. You must in no way say he is covetous.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="34" speaker="First Citizen">If I must not, I need not be barren of accusations;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="35" speaker="First Citizen">he hath faults, with surplus, to tire in repetition.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="36" speaker="First Citizen">What shouts are these? Trust Ye?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="179" speaker="MARCIUS">With every minute you do change a mind,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="180" speaker="MARCIUS">And call him noble that was now your hate,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="181" speaker="MARCIUS">Him vile that was your garland. Friends now fast sworn,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="17" speaker="CORIOLANUS">Whose double bosoms seem to wear one heart,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="18" speaker="CORIOLANUS">Whose house, whose bed, whose meal, and exercise,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="19" speaker="CORIOLANUS">Are still together, who twin, as 'twere, in love</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="20" speaker="CORIOLANUS">Unseparable, shall within this hour,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="21" speaker="CORIOLANUS">On a dissension of a doit, break out</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="22" speaker="CORIOLANUS">To bitterest enmity: so, fellest foes,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="23" speaker="CORIOLANUS">Whose passions and whose plots have broke their sleep,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="24" speaker="CORIOLANUS">To take the one the other, by some chance,</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="25" speaker="CORIOLANUS">Some trick not worth an egg, shall grow dear friends</line><line act="4" scene="4" line="26" speaker="CORIOLANUS">And interjoin their issues. Masters all, be quiet;</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="159" speaker="Third Lord">Put up your swords.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="160" speaker="AUFIDIUS">My lords, when you shall know--as in this rage,</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="161" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Provoked by him, you cannot--the great danger</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="162" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Which this man's life did owe you, you'll rejoice</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="163" speaker="AUFIDIUS">That he is thus cut off. Please it your honours</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="164" speaker="AUFIDIUS">To call me to your senate, I'll deliver</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="165" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Myself your loyal servant, or endure</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="166" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Your heaviest censure.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="167" speaker="First Lord">Bear from hence his body;</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="168" speaker="First Lord">And mourn you for him: let him be regarded</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="169" speaker="First Lord">As the most noble corse that ever herald</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="170" speaker="First Lord">Did follow to his urn.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="171" speaker="Second Lord">His own impatience</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="172" speaker="Second Lord">Takes from Aufidius a great part of blame.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="173" speaker="Second Lord">Let's make the best of it.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="174" speaker="AUFIDIUS">My rage is gone;</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="175" speaker="AUFIDIUS">And I am struck with sorrow. Take him up.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="176" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Help, three o' the chiefest soldiers; I'll be one.</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="177" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Beat thou the drum, that it speak mournfully:</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="178" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Trail your steel pikes. Though in this city he</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="179" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Hath widow'd and unchilded many a one,</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="180" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Which to this hour bewail the injury,</line><line act="5" scene="6" line="181" speaker="AUFIDIUS">Yet he shall have a noble memory.
